Could I have my inner ear removed and relearn how to walk?

Could be useful in lots of situations:

Flying aircraft and not becoming disoriented or sick
Immune to the dizzying effects of flash grenades
Unable to become dizzy in general
???






You could still become dizzy from the visual input (like on a rollercoaster or something).

It could possibly remove the conflict between the inner ear and the visual and avoid getting sick in a moving contained space (such as in a plane) but you don't get dizzy in those anyways.

A much easier method (and an actual realistic one) is to have a surgery to remove your lower esophageal sphincter. This would produce the same effect as people with GERD(I'm among them) experience naturally. At first you'll be sick to your stomach for months but then your brain adapts and you can never, ever get sick again. I can spin myself on a swively chair for hours, ride any rollercoaster or get twisted around in a fighter jet without as much as a burp.

On the downside you'll have daily heartburn for the rest of your life.







You could move them and Im certain you could still walk but you would have to consciously put in constant effort into checking visually that you were still upright and not slanting or about to fall.
